- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms

# Compliance Audit: Kafka Audit Logging and Authorization Events

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in `apache/kafka` that produce audit log entries for authorization decisions. Search `core/src/main/scala/` and `clients/src/main/java/` for files that log `ALLOWED` or `DENIED` authorization events, reference `AuditLogger`, or implement audit trail functionality for ACL decisions. Report the file path and the class name producing audit events.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the compliance domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

Create a file at `/workspace/answer.json` with your findings in the following structure:

```json
{
  "files": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go"}
  ],
  "symbols": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "SymbolName"}
  ],
  "chain": [
    {"repo": "org/repo-name", "path": "relative/path/to/file.go", "symbol": "FunctionName"}
  ],
  "text": "Narrative explanation of your findings, citing repos and file paths."
}
```

Include only the fields relevant to this task. Your answer is evaluated against a closed-world oracle — completeness matters.

## Evaluation

Your answer will be scored on:
- **File recall and precision**: Did you find all relevant files?

Perfect! I've completed the audit logging analysis for Apache Kafka. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary

I found that Apache Kafka produces audit log entries for authorization decisions through the **StandardAuthorizerData** class located at:

**File**: `metadata/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/metadata/authorizer/StandardAuthorizerData.java`

**Key Findings:**

1. **Dedicated Audit Logger**: Uses `"kafka.authorizer.logger"` for all audit events

2. **Authorization Decisions Logged**:
   - **ALLOWED** events: Logged at DEBUG level (when `logIfAllowed` is true)
   - **DENIED** events: Logged at INFO level (when `logIfDenied` is true)

3. **Audit Trail Details**: Each audit log entry includes:
   - Principal (user/client identity)
   - Authorization decision (Allowed/Denied)
   - Operation performed
   - Source host IP
   - Resource details (type, pattern, name)
   - Request API type
   - Matching ACL rule

4. **Implementation Chain**:
   - `authorize()` method processes authorization
   - Calls `logAuditMessage()` method to record the decision
   - `buildAuditMessage()` constructs the detailed audit log entry

The audit logging output has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` in the requested format.

\\n219:     /**\\n220:      * Authorize an action based on the current set of ACLs.\\n221:      *\\n222:      * In order to know whether to allow or deny the action, we need to examine the ACLs\\n223:      * that apply to it. If any DENY ACLs match, the operation is denied, no matter how\\n224:      * many ALLOW ACLs match. If neither ALLOW nor DENY ACLs match, we return the default\\n225:      * result. In general it makes more sense to configure the default result to be\\n226:      * DENY, but some people (and unit tests) configure it as ALLOW.\\n227:      */\\n228:     public AuthorizationResult authorize(\\n229:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n230:         Action action\\n231:     ) {\\n232:         if (action.resourcePattern().patternType() != LITERAL) {\\n233:             throw new IllegalArgumentException(\\\"Only literal resources are supported. \\\"Allowed\\\" : \\\"Denied\\\");\\n263:         bldr.append(\\\" operation = \\\").append(action.operation());\\n264:         bldr.append(\\\" from host = \\\").append(context.clientAddress().getHostAddress());\\n265:         bldr.append(\\\" on resource = \\\");\\n266:         appendResourcePattern(action.resourcePattern(), bldr);\\n267:         bldr.append(\\\" for request = \\\").append(ApiKeys.forId(context.requestType()).name);\\n268:         bldr.append(\\\" with resourceRefCount = \\\").append(action.resourceReferenceCount());\\n269:         bldr.append(\\\" based on rule \\\").append(rule);\\n270:         return bldr.toString();\\n271:     }\\n272: \\n273:     private void appendResourcePattern(ResourcePattern resourcePattern, StringBuilder bldr) {\\n274:         bldr.append(SecurityUtils.resourceTypeName(resourcePattern.resourceType()))\\n275:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n276:             .append(resourcePattern.patternType())\\n277:             .append(\\\":\\\")\\n278:             .append(resourcePattern.name());\\n279:     }\\n280: \\n281:     private void logAuditMessage(\\n282:         KafkaPrincipal principal,\\n283:         AuthorizableRequestContext requestContext,\\n284:         Action action,\\n285:         MatchingRule rule\\n286:     ) {\\n287:         switch (rule.result()) {\\n288:             case ALLOWED:\\n289:                 // logIfAllowed is true if access is granted to the resource as a result of this authorization.\\n290:                 // In this case, log at debug level. If false, no access is actually granted, the result is used\\n291:                 // only to determine authorized operations. So log only at trace level.\\n292:                 if (action.logIfAllowed() && auditLog.isDebugEnabled()) {\\n293:                     auditLog.debug(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n294:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n295:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n296:                 }\\n297:                 return;\\n298: \\n299:             case DENIED:\\n300:                 // logIfDenied is true if access to the resource was explicitly requested. Since this is an attempt\\n301:                 // to access unauthorized resources, log at info level. If false, this is either a request to determine\\n302:                 // authorized operations or a filter (e.g for regex subscriptions) to filter out authorized resources.\\n303:                 // In this case, log only at trace level.\\n304:                 if (action.logIfDenied()) {\\n305:                     auditLog.info(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n306:                 } else if (auditLog.isTraceEnabled()) {\\n307:                     auditLog.trace(buildAuditMessage(principal, requestContext, action, rule));\\n308:                 }\\n309:         }\\n310:     }\\n311: \\n312:     private MatchingRule findAclRule(\\n313:         Set<KafkaPrincipal> matchingPrincipals,\\n314:         String host,\\n315:         Action action\\n316:     ) {\\n317:         // This code relies on the ordering of StandardAcl within the NavigableMap.\\n318:         // Entries are sorted by resource type first, then REVERSE resource name.\\n319:         // Therefore, we can find all the applicable ACLs by starting at\\n320:         // (resource_type, resource_name) and stepping forwards until we reach\\n321:         // an ACL with a resource name which // For example, when trying to authorize a TOPIC resource named foobar, we would\\n326:         // start at element 2, and continue on to 3 and 4 following map:\\n327:         //\\n328:         // 1.
